<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Green Party of England and Wales election results</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>This article lists the <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Elections in the United Kingdom">election results</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party of England and Wales</a> (and its predecessors) in the <a href="/wiki/UK_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="UK parliament">UK parliamentary</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="European parliament">European parliamentary</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh Assembly">Welsh Assembly</a> elections.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_election_2010">General election 2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: General election 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 2010 general election<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> was a milestone for the Green Party as party leader <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Lucas" title="Caroline Lucas">Caroline Lucas</a> was elected Britain's first Green MP in Brighton Pavilion with 31.3% of the vote. The Green Party fielded 310 candidates, six of whom saved their <a href="/wiki/Deposit_(politics)#United_Kingdom" title="Deposit (politics)">deposits</a>. Green candidates came 4th in Norwich South, Hove, Brighton Kemptown, Cambridge and Lewisham Deptford. Overall the Green party received 1.0% of votes in the General election.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_election_2015">General election 2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: General election 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party stood in 571 seats across the UK in the 2015 general election.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> They held Brighton Pavilion and came second place in <a href="/wiki/Bristol_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bristol West (UK Parliament constituency)">Bristol West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Riverside_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Liverpool Riverside (UK Parliament constituency)">Liverpool Riverside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Gorton" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Gorton">Manchester Gorton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Central_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Sheffield Central (UK Parliament constituency)">Sheffield Central</a>, with third places in 17 constituencies.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was the first time the party garnered more than one million votes in a general election.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Deposits were saved in 123 constituencies, where the Green candidate collected at least 5% of the votes cast.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_election_2017">General election 2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: General election 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 2017 general election, Green candidates stood in 457 seats across the UK, standing down in some seats to enable tactical voting. 
</p><p>Deposits were saved in 8 seats: Brighton Pavilion (seat held), Isle of Wight, Buckingham, Bristol West, Sheffield Central, Skipton &amp; Ripon, North Herefordshire and North East Hertfordshire (their sister party, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Green_Party" title="Scottish Green Party">Scottish Green Party</a>, also saved one deposit in Glasgow North). This was down from 123 saved deposits in 2015. The party lost over half its vote compared to 2015, falling from 1,156,149 votes (3.8%) to 524,604 (1.6%). The party also saw significant declines in its share of the vote in target seats, such as in Bristol West (-13.9%), Norwich South (-11%), and Sheffield Central (-7.8%). It also fell behind Labour in the Isle of Wight. In total, the Green vote fell in 561 constituencies, and rose in 22.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By-elections">By-elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: By-elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The party came second in the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Haltemprice_and_Howden_by-election,_2008" title="Haltemprice and Howden by-election, 2008">Haltemprice and Howden by-election</a>, although unusually <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> did not stand candidates.
</p><p>The Richmond Green Party voted against standing in the <a href="/wiki/Richmond_by-election,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Richmond by-election, 2016">2016 Richmond Park by-election</a> and to back the Liberal Democrat candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> On 3 November, the Kingston Green Party did the same, and confirmed that there would not be a Green Party candidate in the by-election.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Party stated that, as a mark of respect, they would not contest the <a href="/wiki/Batley_and_Spen_by-election,_2016" title="Batley and Spen by-election, 2016">2016 Batley and Spen by-election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament_election_2009">European Parliament election 2009</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: European Parliament election 2009">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2009_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2009 (United Kingdom)">European Parliament election, 2009 (United Kingdom)</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2009_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2009 (United Kingdom)">June 2009 European Parliament election</a> the party secured 1,223,303 votes or 7.8% of the popular vote compared to its 2004 vote share of 5.6%. Green MEPs <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Lucas" title="Caroline Lucas">Caroline Lucas</a> in the South East and <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lambert" title="Jean Lambert">Jean Lambert</a> in London were re-elected. The Greens came first in <a href="/wiki/Norwich" title="Norwich">Norwich</a> with 25%, <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a> with 26% and <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove" title="Brighton and Hove">Brighton and Hove</a> with 31%,<sup id="cite_ref-GPEW2009Election_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPEW2009Election-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> but it failed to gain any extra <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEPs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GPEW2009Election1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPEW2009Election1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2018)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The regional breakdown of the vote was as follows:

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament_election_2014">European Parliament election 2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: European Parliament election 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2014 (United Kingdom)">European Parliament election, 2014 (United Kingdom)</a></div>
<p>In the 2014 election, the Greens gained a seat for the first time since 1999, with <a href="/wiki/Molly_Scott_Cato" title="Molly Scott Cato">Molly Scott Cato</a> being elected as MEP for South West England, where the party's vote share rose by 1.8%. However, the party's vote fell in every other region, and there was media speculation that the party had only gained a seat in the South West as a result of <a href="/wiki/An_Independence_from_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="An Independence from Europe">An Independence from Europe</a> dividing the <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UK Independence Party</a> vote.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The regional breakdown of the vote was as follows:

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016">2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In September 2015 <a href="/wiki/Amelia_Womack" title="Amelia Womack">Amelia Womack</a>, Deputy Leader of GPEW, announced her intention to stand in the National Assembly elections for Wales Green Party. <sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Wales Green Party who create their own set of devolved policies around devolved issues in Wales were hopeful of gaining three Assembly seats from the <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> lists in the 2016 elections.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In the event, they won none, their vote share fell by 0.4%, and the party dropped to seventh place, behind the single-issue <a href="/wiki/Abolish_the_Welsh_Assembly_Party" title="Abolish the Welsh Assembly Party">Abolish the Welsh Assembly Party</a>. It was the party's worst result since 1999.
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2011">2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Wales Green Party again fielded candidates in all 5 <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituencies_and_electoral_regions#Electoral_regions" title="National Assembly for Wales constituencies and electoral regions">top-up regions</a> for the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_election,_2011" title="National Assembly for Wales election, 2011">2011 election</a>. For the first time since 1999, the Greens also stood in a constituency - they once again opted to stand in Ceredigion.
</p><p>During the 2011 campaign, they specifically targeted <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Labour_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh Labour Party">Labour</a> voters with the aim of persuading them to use their regional list vote for the Greens, using the slogan "2nd vote Green". They claimed that Labour list votes were "wasted" and that over 70,000 votes in South Wales Central went "in the bin at every election" as Labour had never won a top-up seat in that region.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On this occasion, South Wales Central was the region the party targeted. The region includes Cardiff, with its large student population, and also the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Central_(Assembly_constituency)" title="Cardiff Central (Assembly constituency)">Cardiff Central</a>, the only <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Liberal_Democrats" title="Welsh Liberal Democrats">Liberal Democrat</a>-Labour marginal seat in Wales. Welsh Green leader and South Wales Central candidate Jake Griffiths stated they were also aiming to attract disaffected Liberal Democrat voters in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Greens polled 32,649 votes, 3.4% of the total votes cast for the regional lists.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In South Wales Central, they took over 10,000 votes, 5.2% of the total, though they were still almost 6,000 votes away from winning a seat. The regional results were as follows:

<p>In Ceredigion, Chris Simpson polled 1,514 votes, or 5.2%. He came fifth out of five candidates.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_election,_2007" title="National Assembly for Wales election, 2007">2007</a>, the party again fielded a list of candidates in each of the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituencies_and_electoral_regions#Electoral_regions" title="National Assembly for Wales constituencies and electoral regions">top-up regions</a> but no candidates for the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituencies_and_electoral_regions#Constituencies" title="National Assembly for Wales constituencies and electoral regions">constituencies</a>. The Wales Green Party proposed that Wales should "be at the forefront of....a green industrial revolution". The party targeted South Wales West - the region where they had performed best in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Welsh Greens polled 33,803 votes, or 3.5% of the total, a slight decrease on 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The party failed to win any seats, with their best performance this time being Mid and West Wales with 4.0% of the vote. In South Wales West their vote declined by one percentage point, their worst result of the five regions.
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2003">2003</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2003">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_election,_2003" title="National Assembly for Wales election, 2003">2003 election</a>, the party again fielded a list of candidates for each of the electoral regions but this time stood no candidates for the constituencies. The Welsh Greens failed to win any seats, polling 30,028 votes, or 3.5%. Their best performance was in South Wales West where they polled 6,696 votes, or 4.8% of the total.
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1999">1999</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 1999">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_election,_1999" title="National Assembly for Wales election, 1999">1999 inaugural election for the National Assembly</a>, the Welsh Greens stood candidates in all five <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituencies_and_electoral_regions#Electoral_regions" title="National Assembly for Wales constituencies and electoral regions">electoral regions</a> used to elect "top-up" members of the assembly. Additionally, one candidate stood for the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales_constituencies_and_electoral_regions#Constituencies" title="National Assembly for Wales constituencies and electoral regions">constituency</a> seat of <a href="/wiki/Ceredigion_(Assembly_constituency)" title="Ceredigion (Assembly constituency)">Ceredigion</a>. The party stated that they aimed to poll around 7% of the vote and win at least one top-up seat.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Welsh Greens ultimately polled 25,858 votes in the regional lists, 2.5% of the total, and 1,002 constituency votes (3.1%) in Ceredigion. No Welsh Greens were elected.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UK_Parliament_elections">UK Parliament elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: UK Parliament elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dt>2015</dt></dl>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 UK general election</a>, the Wales Green Party again failed to gain any MPs, but did retain their deposits in three constituencies, having achieved 5% or more of the vote. The party stood candidates in 35 of the 40 constituencies in Wales, far exceeding previous efforts. Leader at the time, Pippa Bartolotti, declared 2015 a 'record breaking year'<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> for the party. The results for the party's candidates in Wales, in alphabetical order of constituency, were as follows:
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Constituency_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituency (UK)">Constituency</a>
</th>
<th>Candidate
</th>
<th>Number of Votes
</th>
<th>Proportion of Votes
</th>
<th><a href="/wiki/Voter_turnout" title="Voter turnout">Turnout</a>
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td width="1" bgcolor="#6AB023">
</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament_elections_2">European Parliament elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: European Parliament elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dt>2014</dt></dl>
<p>The Wales Green Party nominated four candidates for the European Parliament election, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Pippa Bartolotti</li>
<li>John Matthews</li>
<li>Roz Cutler</li>
<li>Christopher Were</li></ul>
<dl><dt>2009</dt></dl>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2009_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2009 (United Kingdom)">European Parliament election, 2009 (United Kingdom)</a>, the Welsh party failed to gain any seats in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, but increased the vote to 5.6% for the four Welsh seats.
</p>
<dl><dt>2004</dt></dl>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/UK_elections,_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="UK elections, 2004">2004 elections</a>, the Welsh party failed to gain any seats in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> (with 3.6% of <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_Election,_2004_(UK)#Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="European Parliament Election, 2004 (UK)">the vote for the four Welsh seats</a>) and lost their only <a href="/wiki/County_council" title="County council">county council</a> seat (of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Klaus_Armstrong-Braun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Klaus Armstrong-Braun (page does not exist)">Klaus Armstrong-Braun</a> in <a href="/wiki/Flintshire" title="Flintshire">Flintshire</a>).
</p>
